True SWAT story. Some 20 years ago, the SWAT team of the Budapest Police Directorate (in Hungary) was sent to apprehend a major drug dealer who was armed and dangerous. He lived in a small condo. A reporter accompanied the SWAT team, whom I happen to know. A decision was made to breach immediately, and disarm the guy before he had a chance to react. The team silently approached the door, they all lined up for the breach, and the commander whispered: "Guys, where's the battering ram?" Turns out they forgot to bring one. Meanwhile, the guy noticed them somehow, climbed out of his window, up to the roof, and vamoosed in the night. Nobody was securing the building from the outside, it was the reporter who noticed the guy climbing up on the gutter. This debacle was one of the reasons why the government detached SWAT operations from the national police and created a professional counter-terrorism agency.

Pro tip:  When breaching a door with a battering ram, always stand on the hinge side before swinging the ram.  Standing on the latch side can result in a broken wrist or forearm since the door will give and the doorframe will not.
Dude.  Seriously?  20 pushups is all it takes to get on SDPD SWAT?  USAF basic training minimum standard in the 1990s was 30.  Pullups, on the other hand, were only 5.  As a Security Policeman, I also had to do the Army PT test annually, because Security Police (now Security Forces) deemed the Air Force PT standards too weak for its members.  The Army standard for pushups and the rest was age based, and I believe it was something like 50 pushups in 2 minutes for my age group (I was in my 20s).  Keep in mind, the Army PT standard was for EVERY troop, regardless of their MOS.  That includes being an army cook.  So, for a SWAT team to require less... that's a bit concerning.  Just saying.
